# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

## Summary

I've created a comprehensive JSON output at `/workspace/answer.json` that identifies all Python source files and validators in django/django that implement model field validation.

### Key Findings:

**Files with Validator Implementations:**
1. `django/core/validators.py` - Core validators (RegexValidator, URLValidator, EmailValidator, MaxLengthValidator, MinValueValidator, etc.)
2. `django/contrib/postgres/validators.py` - PostgreSQL-specific validators (ArrayMaxLengthValidator, RangeMaxValueValidator, etc.)
3. `django/db/models/fields/__init__.py` - Field.clean(), Field.validate(), Field.run_validators()
4. `django/db/models/base.py` - Model validation pipeline (full_clean, clean_fields, validate_unique, validate_constraints)
5. `django/forms/fields.py` - Form field validation

### Validation Pipeline:
The audit documents the complete chain from field validation through to model validation:
- Field.clean() → Field.validate() → Field.run_validators()
- Model.full_clean() → clean_fields() → validate_unique() → validate_constraints()
- Form.full_clean() → _clean_fields() → _clean_form() → _post_clean() (for ModelForms)

Calls clean_fields() for individual field validation\\n  2. Calls clean() for model-wide custom validation\\n  3. Calls validate_unique() for uniqueness constraints\\n  4. Calls to_python() for value conversion\\n  2. Calls validate() for field-level validation\\n  3. Calls run_validators() to execute validators\\n  4. Returns cleaned value\\n\\n- **Field.validate(value)** (line 184): Base implementation checking only the required attribute\\n\\n- **Field.run_validators(value)** (line 188): Executes all validators, aggregating errors\\n\\n## Form Validation (django/forms/forms.py)\\n\\nThe BaseForm class implements the form validation pipeline:\\n\\n- **BaseForm.full_clean()** (line 324): Main entry point that:\\n  1. Initializes error dictionary\\n  2. Calls _clean_fields() to validate individual fields\\n  3. Calls _clean_form() to validate overall form\\n  4. **ModelForm._post_clean()** (line 453+): Calls model.full_clean() with appropriate exclude parameter\\n\\n## Validation Pipeline Summary\\n\\n### Model Instance Validators**: All field validators inherit from BaseValidator or RegexValidator pattern and implement __call__(value) method\\n2. **Validator Discovery**: Fields use default_validators + _validators property to determine which validators to run\\n3. **Error Aggregation**: All validators in run_validators() are executed and errors aggregated before raising ValidationError\\n4. **Model Integration**: Model.clean_fields() calls field.clean() with both value and model instance for context-aware validation\\n5. **Form Integration**: Forms validate fields independently, then optionally
